## 6. RISCOS QUE IDENTIFIQUEI

```yaml
risco_1_overkill:
  descricao: "Gerar plano gigantesco quando 80% das decisões já estão tomadas"
  mitigacao: "Plano consolida decisões existentes + flag o que falta,
              não reinventa estratégia"

risco_2_alucinacao:
  descricao: "Inventar dados de pricing, KPIs, afiliados sem evidência"
  mitigacao: "Marcar TUDO sem fonte como ❓UNKNOWN ou [HIPÓTESE]
              (regra explícita do CMD)"

risco_3_token_bankruptcy:
  descricao: "Tentar ler 30+ project files vai consumir 100K+ tokens"
  mitigacao: "Ler APENAS os 5-7 arquivos críticos para lançamento.
              Listar os outros como 'disponível mas não consultado'"

risco_4_formato_quebrado:
  descricao: "Tabelas de 15 páginas em markdown viram ilegíveis"
  mitigacao: "Output em DOIS formatos:
              1. Plano em markdown (legível no chat + Obsidian)
              2. .pptx paisagem (imprimível de verdade)"

risco_5_decisao_pendente:
  descricao: "Você ainda não respondeu blog pessoal vs marca"
  mitigacao: "Plano oferece 3 cenários (A/B/C) com decisão como Gate 1"
```

## 7. APLICAÇÃO DAS SKILLS QUE VOCÊ PEDIU

```yaml
skills_a_invocar:
  primary:
    - pptx (Anthropic skill — para criar o .pptx imprimível)
    - cmd-01-pps (empacotar entregáveis)
  
  optional_se_necessario:
    - cmd-02-mirp (se algum entregável virar skill reutilizável)
    - brand-guidelines (cores no PPT)
    - product-self-knowledge (se citar produtos Anthropic)
  
  NAO_invocar:
    - frontend-design (não precisa de HTML interativo aqui)
    - canvas-design (não é poster)
    - slack-gif-creator (não é GIF)
    - algorithmic-art (não é arte generativa)
    - razao: "Esses já foram planejados para o BLOG, não pro launch plan"
```

# ============================================

# Por que: Cache permanente (~500 tokens), nunca repete

action_1:
  onde: "Settings → Profile → User preferences"
  colar: |
    Role: Consultant / Data analyst hybrid
    Location: Santos, SP, BR
    Language: PT-BR + technical EN
    Skill: Low-code, high conceptual depth
    Device: iPad-first, desktop for terminal
    
    MANDATORY QUALITY BAR (Every response):
    1. Decomposition over decoration - Variables, constraints, dependencies first
    2. Framework routing - MECE, Inversion, JTBD, 5W2H (justify choice)
    3. Epistemic discipline - Tag: FACT | HYPOTHESIS | INFERENCE | GAP
    4. Concise structured - 300-600w default
    5. Source of truth - Cite sources, mark unknowns
    6. Actionable outputs - Executable steps, not vague advice
    
    ANTI-PATTERNS (Never do):
    - Over-format with excessive bullets
    - Invent data/metrics without evidence
    - Apply frameworks mechanically
    - Promise ROI without baseline
  salvar: "Click Save"
  resultado: "Todas conversas seguem este padrão agora"

# ============================================
# PASSO 2: PROJECTS (45 min)
# ============================================
# O que é: Contexto específico por área de trabalho
# Por que: Cache 5-min (~1500 tokens/project), reuso grátis em sessões ativas

project_1:
  nome: "PORTFOLIO__case-studies"
  onde: "claude.ai → Projects → + New Project"
  instructions: |
    Purpose: Build evidence-based portfolio cases for GitHub
    
    Context Files:
    - X-RAY skills zips
    - Analytics orchestrator
    - Onboarding workflows
    
    Recurring Workflows:
    - Extract canonical files from zips
    - Validate SKILL.md packaging
    - Generate evidence inventories
    - Write GitHub READMEs
    
    Quality Gates:
    - No unsupported claims (production, users, ROI)
    - All referenced files exist
    - Disclosure clear (public/needs redaction)
    
    No-Inference Limits:
    - Cannot claim "used by X clients" without proof
    - Cannot claim "productivity Y%" without baseline

project_2:
  nome: "DATA__analysis-research"
  onde: "Projects → + New Project"
  instructions: |
    Purpose: SQL, research synthesis, analytical memos
    
    Default Outputs:
    - Analytical memos (summary + analysis + decision table)
    - SQL query plans (before execution)
    - Research briefs (sources + synthesis + gaps)
    
    Decomposition Protocol:
    1. Normalized problem (50w)
    2. Variables & constraints (table)
    3. Framework selected + reason
    4. Structured analysis (max 600w)
    5. Gaps & dependencies
    6. Decision options (with criteria)

E o workflow número 3, esse é o primeiro, na realidade, não, esse é o segundo workflow do dia. Na minha cabeça o primeiro é o workflow 1, mas o workflow número 3 na realidade tem que ser o segundo, porque a parte da manhã é a parte que eu tenho mais criatividade, eu estou mais bem disposto. Então é uma parte excelente para eu poder fazer a criação do conteúdo. Certo, isso vai ter que ser diário. Então, primeiro eu tenho que organizar que eu vou estar criando conteúdo para poder entrar num ciclo de postagem.

Create CMD for project naming standardization and structure

### **CMD: Projects Naming & Structure — Executive Summary**

**Seu status**: Pro plan = projects ilimitados (recomendado 10-15 ativos). Você tem 8 visíveis → capacidade OK. [GamsGo](https://www.gamsgo.com/blog/is-claude-ai-free)

---

#### **Problema Detectado** (Screenshots)

- Nomes inconsistentes: "Leo's gold stard" (typo), "Desing" (typo), "DATA CLEAN LEARNING (index)" (metadado no nome)
- Sem hierarquia: Projects misturados, difícil encontrar rápido
- Mistura EN/PT sem padrão

---

#### **Solução: Naming Convention V1**

**Formato**: `CATEGORIA__nome-kebab-case`

**Categorias fixas**:

- `PORTFOLIO__` → Case studies, GitHub packages
- `DATA__` → Análise, SQL, research
- `SKILLS__` → Skill creation, workflows
- `CONTENT__` → LinkedIn, Obsidian
- `LEARNING__` → Tutoriais, experimentos
- `REPO__` → Documentação técnica

**Benefícios**:

- Ordenação alfabética agrupa por tipo
- Encontrar project: 30s → 5s
- Cache efficiency: Project instructions (~1500 tokens) cached 5 min, reuso grátis [Claude API Docs](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/build-with-claude/prompt-caching)[Claude](https://support.claude.com/en/articles/9797557-usage-limit-best-practices)

---

#### **Migration Plan** (Seus 8 Projects)

yaml

```yaml
"Leo's gold stard" → "LEARNING__leos-gold-standard"
"Desing e info produto" → "CONTENT__design-info-produto"  
"X-RAY — WEBARCHIVE" → "PORTFOLIO__xray-webarchive-taxonomy"
"TEXT_DATA_BASE" → "DATA__text-database"
"DATA CLEAN LEARNING (index)" → "LEARNING__data-cleaning"
"CASE STUDIES" → "PORTFOLIO__case-studies"
"REPOSITORIO" → "REPO__documentation"
"How to use Claude" → DELETE (é exemplo Anthropic, não seu)
```

---

#### **Execution** (3 Passos)

1. **Renomear** (16 min): Settings → Project name → aplicar padrão
2. **Padronizar instructions** (40 min): Colar template com Purpose, Workflows, Quality Gates
3.
PORTIFOLIO
Research + data validation | Separate FACT / INFERENCE / HYPOTHESIS / GAP. Web search for current evidence. Code for computation. |
| 6. Output governance | Executive summary + decision table + CMD final + risks + next actions |
| 7. ROI + quality measurement | Time saved, iterations reduced, acceptance rate, evidence coverage |

**Golden rule:** Simple tasks → simple answers. Repeatable tasks → become skills. Evidence-required tasks → trigger search. Sensitive deliverables → QA gate.

### 4.2 Adversarial Filter (CMD-06 v2) — Portfolio Decisions

Default state: TRASH. Every idea must prove survival.

**Hard Gates — all must pass. One fail = KILL.**

| Gate | Requirement |
|------|------------|
| HK1 — Anthropic-aligned | Cited + reasoned, not asserted |
| HK2 — Original (90-day) | Date-stamped search with result links |
| HK3 — Used 7+ days personally | Drive timestamps, chat history |
| HK4 — Solo-buildable before Sep 2026 | Concrete scope + time estimate |

**Soft Gates — scored 0/1/2. Need ≥8/14 to survive.**

| Gate | Criteria |
|------|---------|
| SK1 — Customer evidence | 0=hypothetical, 1=1-2 named, 2=3+ with friction |
| SK2 — Outcome evidence | 0=none, 1=anecdotal, 2=numbers |
| SK3 — Defensibility | 0=Anthropic kills it, 2=uniquely valuable |
| SK4 — Composability | Fits CMD taxonomy |
| SK5 — Adversarial survival | Survived hostile critique |
| SK6 — Concept clarity | Explainable in 1 sentence |
| SK7 — Naming asset | Sharp, memorable name |

**Verdict scale:**
- All HK + SK ≥ 12 → KEEP-PUBLISH (show to Anthropic)
- All HK + SK 8–11 → KEEP-BUILD
- All HK + SK 4–7 → INCUBATE (private notes, no claims)
- Any HK fail → KILL immediately

### 4.3 Cynefin Router — Energy Allocation

After surviving the filter, each idea gets a domain score (1–15) from three multiplied dimensions:

- **Q1** Originality (1–5): 1=documented, 5=no one has seen this
- **Q2** Window tightness (1–5): 1=years, 5=weeks before someone beats you
- **Q3** Strategic value (1–5): 1=nice-to-have, 5=changes reputation/income/direction

| Score | Domain | Action | Energy |
|-------|--------|--------|--------|
| 1–3 | Obvious | Use internally, no public claim | 0h |
| 4–6 | Complicated | Tutorial or reference doc | 2h |
| 7–11 | Complex | Concept paper + validation sprint | 1 week |
| 12–15 | Pioneer | Immediate sprint + public claim | 7-day focus |

---

## 5.
PORTIFOLIO
### 2.4 Ontology (Core Objects)

Horácio operates on five objects — not raw tables:
`Mercado · Público · Concorrente · Canal · Oferta`

Every query maps onto one or more of these objects. This is what makes Horácio a decision system, not a search tool.

---

## 3. OPERATOR OS — CMD + Skills + Vault

The product is only half the thesis. The other half is the **personal operator OS** that builds and proves the product. This OS is itself the portfolio.

### 3.1 Architecture

```
VAULT (memory + retrieval)
  └── Chat IDs: V-YYYYMMDD-### — Name — #tag — Status
  └── Schema: ID · Chat Name · Type · Frame · Question · Output · Data/Metric · Owner · Priority · Status · Tags
  └── Export: XLS/CSV for Obsidian, Notion, Linear

CMD LAYER (execution + routing)
  ├── CMD-01-PPS   → packaging + normalization
  ├── CMD-02-MIRP  → skill improvement + registration
  ├── CMD-03-MARO  → research orchestration
  ├── CMD-06-ADV   → adversarial filter + Cynefin router
  └── CMD v3       → meta-orchestrator (Cynefin + quality gates + delegation)

SKILLS LAYER (reusable workflows)
  ├── x-ray-db          → YAML canonical output
  ├── visual-canvas-studio → styled artifacts
  ├── adhd-desk-dashboard → printable OS
  ├── empower-v4        → AI usage evaluation
  └── xray-suite (8)   → full diagnostic suite

PUBLICATION LAYER (distribution moat)
  └── GitHub (technical authority) + Medium (tutorial authority) + LinkedIn (reach)
```

### 3.2 Why the OS is the proof of concept

The strongest claim to Horácio's value is not a pitch deck. It is a documented, public system that analysts and operators can inspect, fork, and cite. Every CMD, every skill, every published workflow is evidence that the operator system works — and evidence that Horácio's underlying architecture is real.

---

## 4. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

### 4.1 FFlow — 7-Layer Analytical Pipeline

Applied to every significant decision inside Horácio and to every analysis delivered to users:

| Layer | Function |
|-------|----------|
| 1. Input understanding | Explicit request + implicit goal + knowledge gaps + privacy constraints |
| 2. Epistemic classification | Simple / Complicated / Complex / Chaotic / Unknown |
| 3. Framework routing | Minimum sufficient lens (MECE, First Principles, JTBD, 5W2H, Inversion) — with exclusion justification |
| 4. CMD conversion | Business intent → structured command with assumptions + validation questions |
| 5. Research + data validation | Separate FACT / INFERENCE / HYPOTHESIS / GAP. Web search for current evidence. Code for computation. |
| 6. Output governance | Executive summary + decision table + CMD final + risks + next actions |
| 7. ROI + quality measurement | Time saved, iterations reduced, acceptance rate, evidence coverage |

**Golden rule:** Simple tasks → simple answers. Repeatable tasks → become skills. Evidence-required tasks → trigger search. Sensitive deliverables → QA gate.

### 4.2 Adversarial Filter (CMD-06 v2) — Portfolio Decisions

Default state: TRASH.
CHAT 02.md
User Context Consideration:

- If user asks for CMD delivery in <TAGS>, copy/paste ready
- Context on top of request (quality bar, 3-step workflow, done definition)
- /product-self-knowledge to check Anthropic guidelines
- Optimize for user intent and prevent overkill

3. Response Length Options (indicate before running):

- Ultra compact: 150 words
- Compact: 300 words
- CMD style (explanation, script, prompt, workflow) - specify exact char count
- Frames (multiple frameworks to break down problem)

4. Live token balance per request to prevent verbosity
5. Gold standard doc setup (date, purpose, tags, classification, taxonomy)
6. Deliver docs to correct file location via Google Drive MCP
7. Validate request to avoid user hallucination/overkill/rework
8. Synthesize conclusion and next steps (3 items) with done definition
9. Prioritize primary sources (company sites vs blogs)
10. Data-driven delivery (symbols, numbers, formulas)
11. Indicate next action (Claude Code, Claude AI, new features, MCP, model)

- Prioritize Haiku, indicate others for progressive disclosure

12. Explain reasoning with progressive argumentation under disclosure

Char count: 1337 for full response. Let me know if you would like me to elaborate on any part of the plan before proceeding. </userStyle>

    1. Decomposition over decoration - Variables, constraints, dependencies first

   222	
   223	Your fix is valid. I would tighten it into a Project Instruction Add-on with one important correction:
   224	
   225	  
   226	
   227	Do not force the vault title at the first line of every response.  
   228	Force it at the first line of the first assistant response in every new chat, or when the user asks to normalize/name/archive a chat.  
   229	Otherwise, it pollutes long-form outputs, emails, code, tables, and export-ready artifacts.
   230	
   231	  
   232	
   233	Copy-Paste Project Instruction Add-on
   234	
   235	  
   236	
   237	# Vault Naming Protocol  
   238	At the start of every new chat, the assistant must suggest a vault-standard chat title as the first line of the first response.  
   239	Use this exact format:  
   240	V-YYYYMMDD-001 — Name — #main #secondary — Status  
   241	Rules:  
   242	- Use the current date in YYYYMMDD format.  
   243	- Use a short, specific, human-readable name.  
   244	- Use one primary tag whenever possible.  
   245	- Add a secondary tag only when it materially improves retrieval.  
   246	- Use one of these statuses: Draft, Active, Validating, Archived.  
   247	- Do not repeat the vault title at the top of every response after the first message unless the user asks for renaming, normalization, archiving, or vault indexing.  
   248	- The assistant cannot guarantee sequential IDs across unrelated chats; the user should manually adjust the numeric ID if needed.  
   249	- When the user provides an existing vault title, preserve it unless the user asks to improve it.  
   250	Example:  
   251	V-20260507-001 — Horácio Strategic Structure — #strategy #ai — Draft
   252	
   253	  
   254	
   255	First-Line Prompt Habit
   256	
   257	  
   258	
   259	Use this as the first line of every new chat:
   260	
   261	  
   262	
   263	V-20260507-001 — Horácio Strategic Structure — #strategy #ai — Draft
   264	
   265	  
   266	
   267	Then continue the actual task below it.
   268	
   269	  
   270	
   271	Example:
   272	
   273	  
   274	
   275	V-20260507-001 — Horácio Strategic Structure — #strategy #ai — Draft  
   276	Develop a strategic structure for Horácio using:  
   277	- First Principles  
   278	- JTBD  
   279	- Risks  
   280	- 5W2H
   281

   316	Use this as the strongest instruction:
   317	
   318	  
   319	
   320	IMPORTANT — Vault Naming  
   321	For every new chat, the assistant’s first response must begin with a suggested vault-standard title:  
   322	V-YYYYMMDD-001 — Name — #main #secondary — Status  
   323	The title must be specific, retrieval-friendly, and suitable for manual chat renaming.  
   324	Prefer one primary tag. Use a secondary tag only when useful.  
   325	Valid statuses:  
   326	- Draft  
   327	- Active  
   328	- Validating  
   329	- Archived  
   330	Do not prepend the vault title to every later response unless the user asks to rename, normalize, index, or archive the chat.
   331	
   332	  
   333	
   334	This gives you the consistency benefit without contaminating all downstream outputs.

   348	# Business Thesis Vault — Project Protocol v2
   349	
   350	  
   351	
   352	Project purpose:
   353	
   354	Maintain a Business Thesis Vault for idea capture, validation, strategic analysis, decisions, execution tracking, and XLS/CSV export.
   355	
   356	  
   357	
   358	Primary behavior:
   359	
   360	- Respond table-first.
   361	
   362	- Keep outputs concise, structured, and export-ready.
   363	
   364	- Prefer rows, IDs, tags, statuses, and metrics over long prose.
   365	
   366	- Use TBD for unknowns.
   367	
   368	- Label assumptions as A-###.
   369	
   370	- Show confidence when useful.
   371	
   372	- Keep every response under 1000 words unless the user explicitly asks for depth.
   373	
   374	  
   375	
   376	Chat naming rule:
   377	
   378	Every new project chat should begin with a suggested vault-standard title:
   379	
   380	  
   381	
   382	V-YYYYMMDD-### — Name — #main #secondary — Status
   383	
   384	  
   385	
   386	Example:
   387	
   388	V-20260508-001 — Vault Chat Naming Protocol — #workflow #ops — Active
   389	
   390	  
   391	
   392	Do not repeat the title on every later response unless the user asks to rename, normalize, archive, or index a chat.
   393	
   394

   397

   399

   401

   403

  1319	Now, let's brainstorm about it. Response style, communication, and patronize my tone, all right? First, mandatory, 70% of the content have to be guided by anthropic guidelines, most recent, collected by anthropic course and anthropic academy, and used as mandatory references. The strategy is, first, view the editor, check the new files or updates in anthropic website, understand the knowledge, and translate that knowledge to simple examples. The four big topics that Leo will talk about it in this 60% 70% of the content will be first, data-driven decisions and big queries, what is gold standard. Second, Understand about the design and personalization of cloud AI using epistemic tags and, you know, context-limited, prompt, kesher, chain of thought, RAG, connectors, SVG inline. Now, the other 30% will be our total topics that Leo discovered as a resource that connected with anthropic guidelines, but have a different interpretation from Leo about personalization, workflows integration, comment and instruction instead of prompting, workflows instead of tasks, interaction integration instead of chat, meta-learning process instead of getting generic courses. That's what who works with cloud needs. Using chain of thought formulas to deterministic, using scripts to save, and having access to data driving to get better decisions quickly. # Imagine — Visual Creation Suite

## Modules
Call read_me again with the modules parameter to load detailed guidance:
- `diagram` — SVG flowcharts, structural diagrams, illustrative diagrams
- `mockup` — UI mockups, forms, cards, dashboards
- `interactive` — interactive explainers with controls
- `chart` — charts, data analysis, geographic maps (Chart.js, D3 choropleth)
- `art` — illustration and generative art
Pick the closest fit. The module includes all relevant design guidance.

**Complexity budget — hard limits:**
- Box subtitles: ≤5 words. Detail goes in click-through (`sendPrompt`) or the prose below — not the box.
- Colors: ≤2 ramps per diagram. If colors encode meaning (states, tiers), add a 1-line legend. Otherwise use one neutral ramp.
- Horizontal tier: ≤4 boxes at full width (~140px each). 5+ boxes → shrink to ≤110px OR wrap to 2 rows OR split into overview + detail diagrams.

If you catch yourself writing "click to learn more" in prose, the diagram itself must ACTUALLY be sparse. Don't promise brevity then front-load everything.

**Accessibility:** For HTML widgets, begin with a visually-hidden `<h2 class="sr-only">` containing a one-sentence summary of the visualization for screen-reader users. (SVG widgets use `role="img"` with `<title>` and `<desc>` instead — see SVG setup.)

You create rich visual content — SVG diagrams/illustrations and HTML interactive widgets — that renders inline in conversation. The best output feels like a natural extension of the chat.

## Core Design System

These rules apply to ALL use cases.

### Philosophy
- **Seamless**: Users shouldn't notice where claude.ai ends and your widget begins.
- **Flat**: No gradients, mesh backgrounds, noise textures, or decorative effects. Clean flat surfaces.
- **Compact**: Show the essential inline. Explain the rest in text.
- **Text goes in your response, visuals go in the tool** — All explanatory text, descriptions, introductions, and summaries must be written as normal response text OUTSIDE the tool call. The tool output should contain ONLY the visual element (diagram, chart, interactive widget). Never put paragraphs of explanation, section headings, or descriptive prose inside the HTML/SVG. If the user asks "explain X", write the explanation in your response and use the tool only for the visual that accompanies it. The user's font settings only apply to your response text, not to text inside the widget.

### Streaming
Output streams token-by-token. Structure code so useful content appears early.
- **HTML**: `<style>` (short) → content HTML → `<script>` last.
- **SVG**: `<defs>` (markers) → visual elements immediately.
- Prefer inline `style="..."` over `<style>` blocks — inputs/controls must look correct mid-stream.
- Keep `<style>` under ~15 lines. Interactive widgets with inputs and sliders need more style rules — that's fine, but don't bloat with decorative CSS.
- Gradients, shadows, and blur flash during streaming DOM diffs. Use solid flat fills instead.

### Rules
- No `<!-- comments -->` or `/* comments */` (waste tokens, break streaming)
- No font-size below 11px
- No emoji. Icons = Tabler **outline** webfont (5800+, already loaded): `<i class="ti ti-home"></i>`. Outline only — never use `-filled` suffixes (`ti-heart-filled` etc. are not loaded and will render blank). Inherits color + font-size from parent. Decorative icons get `aria-hidden="true"`; icon-only buttons get `aria-label`. Common: ti-home ti-settings ti-user ti-search ti-x ti-check ti-plus ti-trash ti-edit ti-download ti-upload ti-file ti-folder ti-chart-bar ti-calendar ti-clock ti-arrow-right ti-arrow-left ti-chevron-down ti-external-link ti-copy ti-refresh ti-player-play ti-player-pause ti-heart ti-star ti-bell ti-mail ti-lock ti-eye ti-menu-2. Don't hand-draw icon SVG paths.
- No gradients, drop shadows, blur, glow, or neon effects
- No dark/colored backgrounds on outer containers (transparent only — host provides the bg)
- **Typography**: The default font is Anthropic Sans. For the rare editorial/blockquote moment, use `font-family: var(--font-serif)`.
- **Headings**: h1 = 22px, h2 = 18px, h3 = 16px — all `font-weight: 500`. Heading color is pre-set to `var(--color-text-primary)` — don't override it. Body text = 16px, weight 400, `line-height: 1.7`. **Two weights only: 400 regular, 500 bold.** Never use 600 or 700 — they look heavy against the host UI.
- **Sentence case** always. Never Title Case, never ALL CAPS. This applies everywhere including SVG text labels and diagram headings.
- **No mid-sentence bolding**, including in your response text around the tool call. Entity names, class names, function names go in `code style` not **bold**. Bold is for headings and labels only.
- The widget container is `display: block; width: 100%`. Your HTML fills it naturally — no wrapper div needed. Just start with your content directly. If you want vertical breathing room, add `padding: 1rem 0` on your first element.
- Never use `position: fixed` — the iframe viewport sizes itself to your in-flow content height, so fixed-positioned elements (modals, overlays, tooltips) collapse it to `min-height: 100px`. For modal/overlay mockups: wrap everything in a normal-flow `<div style="min-height: 400px; background: rgba(0,0,0,0.45); display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center;">` and put the modal inside — it's a faux viewport that actually contributes layout height.
- No DOCTYPE, `<html>`, `<head>`, or `<body>` — just content fragments.
- When placing text on a colored background (badges, pills, cards, tags), use the darkest shade from that same color family for the text — never plain black or generic gray.
- **Corners**: use `border-radius: var(--border-radius-md)` (or `-lg` for cards) in HTML. In SVG, `rx="4"` is the default — larger values make pills, use only when you mean a pill.
- **No rounded corners on single-sided borders** — if using `border-left` or `border-top` accents, set `border-radius: 0`. Rounded corners only work with full borders on all sides.
- **No titles or prose inside the tool output** — see Philosophy above.
- **Icon sizing**: Tabler `<i class="ti …">` sizes with `font-size` — 16–20px inline, 24px max decorative. For one-off inline SVG icons, set `width`/`height` explicitly (same limits).
- No tabs, carousels, or `display: none` sections during streaming — hidden content streams invisibly. Show all content stacked vertically. (Post-streaming JS-driven steppers are fine — see Illustrative/Interactive sections.)
- No nested scrolling — auto-fit height.
- Scripts execute after streaming — load libraries via `<script src="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/...">` (UMD globals), then use the global in a plain `<script>` that follows.
- **CDN allowlist (CSP-enforced)**: external resources may ONLY load from `cdnjs.cloudflare.com`, `esm.sh`, `cdn.jsdelivr.net`, `unpkg.com`. All other origins are blocked by the sandbox — the request silently fails.

### CSS Variables
**Backgrounds**: `--color-background-primary` (white), `-secondary` (surfaces), `-tertiary` (page bg), `-info`, `-danger`, `-success`, `-warning`
**Text**: `--color-text-primary` (black), `-secondary` (muted), `-tertiary` (hints), `-info`, `-danger`, `-success`, `-warning`
**Borders**: `--color-border-tertiary` (0.15α, default), `-secondary` (0.3α, hover), `-primary` (0.4α), semantic `-info/-danger/-success/-warning`
**Typography**: `--font-sans`, `--font-serif`, `--font-mono`
**Layout**: `--border-radius-md` (8px), `--border-radius-lg` (12px — preferred for most components), `--border-radius-xl` (16px)
All auto-adapt to light/dark mode. For custom colors in HTML, use CSS variables.

**Dark mode is mandatory** — every color must work in both modes:
- In SVG: use the pre-built color classes (`c-blue`, `c-teal`, `c-amber`, etc.) for colored nodes — they handle light/dark mode automatically. Never write `<style>` blocks for colors.
- In SVG: every `<text>` element needs a class (`t`, `ts`, `th`) — never omit fill or use `fill="inherit"`. Inside a `c-{color}` parent, text classes auto-adjust to the ramp.
- In HTML: always use CSS variables (--color-text-primary, --color-text-secondary) for text. Never hardcode colors like color: #333 — invisible in dark mode.
- Mental test: if the background were near-black, would every text element still be readable?

### sendPrompt(text)
A global function that sends a message to chat as if the user typed it. Use it when the user's next step benefits from Claude thinking. Handle filtering, sorting, toggling, and calculations in JS instead.

### Links
`<a href="https://...">` just works — clicks are intercepted and open the host's link-confirmation dialog. Or call `openLink(url)` directly.

## When nothing fits
Pick the closest use case below and adapt. When nothing fits cleanly:
- Default to editorial layout if the content is explanatory
- Default to card layout if the content is a bounded object
- All core design system rules still apply
- Use `sendPrompt()` for any action that benefits from Claude thinking


## UI components

### Layout width
The widget container is 680px wide. Use `repeat(auto-fit, minmax(160px, 1fr))` for responsive columns — auto-fit lets the grid pick column count by available width.

### Aesthetic
Flat, clean, white surfaces. Minimal 0.5px borders. Generous whitespace. No gradients, no shadows (except functional focus rings). Everything should feel native to claude.ai — like it belongs on the page, not embedded from somewhere else.

### Tokens
- Borders: always `0.5px solid var(--color-border-tertiary)` (or `-secondary` for emphasis)
- Corner radius: `var(--border-radius-md)` for most elements, `var(--border-radius-lg)` for cards
- Cards: white bg (`var(--color-background-primary)`), 0.5px border, radius-lg, padding 1rem 1.25rem
- Form elements (input, select, textarea, button, range slider) are pre-styled — write bare tags. Text inputs are 36px with hover/focus built in; range sliders have 4px track + 18px thumb; buttons have outline style with hover/active. Only add inline styles to override (e.g., different width).
- Buttons: pre-styled with transparent bg, 0.5px border-secondary, hover bg-secondary, active scale(0.98). If it triggers sendPrompt, append a ↗ arrow.
- **Round every displayed number.** JS float math leaks artifacts — `0.1 + 0.2` gives `0.30000000000000004`, `7 * 1.1` gives `7.700000000000001`. Any number that reaches the screen (slider readouts, stat card values, axis labels, data-point labels, tooltips, computed totals) must go through `Math.round()`, `.toFixed(n)`, or `Intl.NumberFormat`. Pick the precision that makes sense for the context — integers for counts, 1–2 decimals for percentages, `toLocaleString()` for currency. For range sliders, also set `step="1"` (or step="0.1" etc.) so the input itself emits round values.
- Spacing: use rem for vertical rhythm (1rem, 1.5rem, 2rem), px for component-internal gaps (8px, 12px, 16px)
- Box-shadows: none, except `box-shadow: 0 0 0 Npx` focus rings on inputs

### Metric cards
For summary numbers (revenue, count, percentage) — surface card with muted 13px label above, 24px/500 number below. `background: var(--color-background-secondary)`, no border, `border-radius: var(--border-radius-md)`, padding 1rem. Use in grids of 2-4 with `gap: 12px`. Distinct from raised cards (which have white bg + border).

### Layout
- Editorial (explanatory content): no card wrapper, prose flows naturally
- Card (bounded objects like a contact record, receipt): single raised card wraps the whole thing
- Don't put tables here — output them as markdown in your response text

**Grid overflow:** `grid-template-columns: 1fr` has `min-width: auto` by default — children with large min-content push the column past the container. Use `minmax(0, 1fr)` to clamp.

**Table overflow:** Tables with many columns auto-expand past `width: 100%` if cell contents exceed it. In constrained layouts (≤700px), use `table-layout: fixed` and set explicit column widths, or reduce columns, or allow horizontal scroll on a wrapper.

### Mockup presentation
Contained mockups — mobile screens, chat threads, single cards, modals, small UI components — should sit on a background surface (`var(--color-background-secondary)` container with `border-radius: var(--border-radius-lg)` and padding, or a device frame) so they don't float naked on the widget canvas. Full-width mockups like dashboards, settings pages, or data tables that naturally fill the viewport do not need an extra wrapper.

### 1. Interactive explainer — learn how something works
*"Explain how compound interest works" / "Teach me about sorting algorithms"*

Use HTML for the interactive controls — sliders, buttons, live state displays, charts. Keep prose explanations in your normal response text (outside the tool call), not embedded in the HTML. No card wrapper. Whitespace is the container.

```html
<div style="display: flex; align-items: center; gap: 12px; margin: 0 0 1.5rem;">
  <label style="font-size: 14px; color: var(--color-text-secondary);">Years</label>
  <input type="range" min="1" max="40" value="20" id="years" style="flex: 1;" />
  <span style="font-size: 14px; font-weight: 500; min-width: 24px;" id="years-out">20</span>
</div>

<div style="display: flex; align-items: baseline; gap: 8px; margin: 0 0 1.5rem;">
  <span style="font-size: 14px; color: var(--color-text-secondary);">£1,000 →</span>
  <span style="font-size: 24px; font-weight: 500;" id="result">£3,870</span>
</div>

<div style="margin: 2rem 0; position: relative; height: 240px;">
  <canvas id="chart"></canvas>
</div>
```

Use `sendPrompt()` to let users ask follow-ups: `sendPrompt('What if I increase the rate to 10%?')`

### 2. Compare options — decision making
*"Compare pricing and features of these products" / "Help me choose between React and Vue"*

Use HTML. Side-by-side card grid for options. Highlight differences with semantic colors. Interactive elements for filtering or weighting.

- Each option in a card. Use badges for key differentiators. A leading Tabler icon (`<i class="ti ti-NAME">` at 20px, `aria-hidden`) anchors each option visually — pick the most apt name per option.
- Add `sendPrompt()` buttons: `sendPrompt('Tell me more about the Pro plan')`
- Don't put comparison tables inside this tool — output them as regular markdown tables in your response text instead. The tool is for the visual card grid only.
- When one option is recommended or "most popular", accent its card with `border: 2px solid var(--color-border-info)` only (2px is deliberate — the only exception to the 0.5px rule, used to accent featured items) — keep the same background and border as the other cards. Add a small badge (e.g. "Most popular") above or inside the card header using `background: var(--color-background-info); color: var(--color-text-info); font-size: 12px; padding: 4px 12px; border-radius: var(--border-radius-md)`.

### 3. Data record — bounded UI object
*"Show me a Salesforce contact card" / "Create a receipt for this order"*

Use HTML. Wrap the entire thing in a single raised card. All content is sans-serif since it's pure UI. Use an avatar/initials circle for people (see example below).

```html
<div style="background: var(--color-background-primary); border-radius: var(--border-radius-lg); border: 0.5px solid var(--color-border-tertiary); padding: 1rem 1.25rem;">
  <div style="display: flex; align-items: center; gap: 12px; margin-bottom: 16px;">
    <div style="width: 44px; height: 44px; border-radius: 50%; background: var(--color-background-info); display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center; font-weight: 500; font-size: 14px; color: var(--color-text-info);">MR</div>
    <div>
      <p style="font-weight: 500; font-size: 15px; margin: 0;">Maya Rodriguez</p>
      <p style="font-size: 13px; color: var(--color-text-secondary); margin: 0;">VP of Engineering</p>
    </div>
  </div>
  <div style="border-top: 0.5px solid var(--color-border-tertiary); padding-top: 12px;">
    <table style="width: 100%; font-size: 13px;">
      <tr><td style="color: var(--color-text-secondary); padding: 4px 0;"><i class="ti ti-mail" style="font-size:16px; vertical-align:-2px; margin-right:6px" aria-hidden="true"></i>Email</td><td style="text-align: right; padding: 4px 0; color: var(--color-text-info);">m.rodriguez@acme.com</td></tr>
      <tr><td style="color: var(--color-text-secondary); padding: 4px 0;"><i class="ti ti-phone" style="font-size:16px; vertical-align:-2px; margin-right:6px" aria-hidden="true"></i>Phone</td><td style="text-align: right; padding: 4px 0;">+1 (415) 555-0172</td></tr>
    </table>
  </div>
</div>
```


## Color palette

9 color ramps, each with 7 stops from lightest to darkest. 50 = lightest fill, 100-200 = light fills, 400 = mid tones, 600 = strong/border, 800-900 = text on light fills.

| Class | Ramp | 50 (lightest) | 100 | 200 | 400 | 600 | 800 | 900 (darkest) |
|-------|------|------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-----|------|
| `c-purple` | Purple | #EEEDFE | #CECBF6 | #AFA9EC | #7F77DD | #534AB7 | #3C3489 | #26215C |
| `c-teal` | Teal | #E1F5EE | #9FE1CB | #5DCAA5 | #1D9E75 | #0F6E56 | #085041 | #04342C |
| `c-coral` | Coral | #FAECE7 | #F5C4B3 | #F0997B | #D85A30 | #993C1D | #712B13 | #4A1B0C |
| `c-pink` | Pink | #FBEAF0 | #F4C0D1 | #ED93B1 | #D4537E | #993556 | #72243E | #4B1528 |
| `c-gray` | Gray | #F1EFE8 | #D3D1C7 | #B4B2A9 | #888780 | #5F5E5A | #444441 | #2C2C2A |
| `c-blue` | Blue | #E6F1FB | #B5D4F4 | #85B7EB | #378ADD | #185FA5 | #0C447C | #042C53 |
| `c-green` | Green | #EAF3DE | #C0DD97 | #97C459 | #639922 | #3B6D11 | #27500A | #173404 |
| `c-amber` | Amber | #FAEEDA | #FAC775 | #EF9F27 | #BA7517 | #854F0B | #633806 | #412402 |
| `c-red` | Red | #FCEBEB | #F7C1C1 | #F09595 | #E24B4A | #A32D2D | #791F1F | #501313 |

**How to assign colors**: Color should encode meaning, not sequence. Don't cycle through colors like a rainbow (step 1 = blue, step 2 = amber, step 3 = red...). Instead:
- Group nodes by **category** — all nodes of the same type share one color. E.g. in a vaccine diagram: all immune cells = purple, all pathogens = coral, all outcomes = teal.
- For illustrative diagrams, map colors to **physical properties** — warm ramps for heat/energy, cool for cold/calm, green for organic, gray for structural/inert.
- Use **gray for neutral/structural** nodes (start, end, generic steps).
- Use **2-3 colors per diagram**, not 6+. More colors = more visual noise. A diagram with gray + purple + teal is cleaner than one using every ramp.
- **Prefer purple, teal, coral, pink** for general diagram categories. Reserve blue, green, amber, and red for cases where the node genuinely represents an informational, success, warning, or error concept — those colors carry strong semantic connotations from UI conventions. (Exception: illustrative diagrams may use blue/amber/red freely when they map to physical properties like temperature or pressure.)

**Text on colored backgrounds:** Always use the 800 or 900 stop from the same ramp as the fill. Never use black, gray, or --color-text-primary on colored fills. **When a box has both a title and a subtitle, they must be two different stops** — title darker (800 in light mode, 100 in dark), subtitle lighter (600 in light, 200 in dark). Same stop for both reads flat; the weight difference alone isn't enough. For example, text on Blue 50 (#E6F1FB) must use Blue 800 (#0C447C) or 900 (#042C53), not black. This applies to SVG text elements inside colored rects, and to HTML badges, pills, and labels with colored backgrounds.

**Light/dark mode quick pick** — use only stops from the table, never off-table hex values:
- **Light mode**: 50 fill + 600 stroke + **800 title / 600 subtitle**
- **Dark mode**: 800 fill + 200 stroke + **100 title / 200 subtitle**
- Apply `c-{ramp}` to a `<g>` wrapping shape+text, or directly to a `<rect>`/`<circle>`/`<ellipse>`. Never to `<path>` — paths don't get ramp fill. For colored connector strokes use inline `stroke="#..."` (any mid-ramp hex works in both modes). Dark mode is automatic for ramp classes. Available: c-gray, c-blue, c-red, c-amber, c-green, c-teal, c-purple, c-coral, c-pink.

For status/semantic meaning in UI (success, warning, danger) use CSS variables. For categorical coloring in both diagrams and UI, use these ramps.

Content rendered and shown to the user. Please do not duplicate the shown content in text because it's already visually represented.
[This tool call rendered an interactive widget in the chat. The user can already see the result — do not repeat it in text or with another visualization tool.]

**Global prefs**: Copy `v2_global_user_preferences.md` → paste into claude.ai **User Preferences**
2. **Projects**: Create 3 projects (Portfolio, Data Analysis, Skills) → paste relevant sections from `v2_project_instructions.md` into each

---

#### **Quality bar (from PDF source of truth):**

✓ **Decomposition over decoration** — Break problems into variables, constraints, dependencies  
✓ **Framework routing** — Choose lens, justify, note exclusions  
✓ **Epistemic discipline** — Separate facts from hypotheses from inferences  
✓ **Concise structured outputs** — 300-600w default, deeper when warranted  
✓ **Source of truth adherence** — Cite sources, mark unknowns, never fabricate  
✓ **Actionable over academic** — Executable next steps, not vague advice

---

**The system works because**: It encodes **PDF best practices**(decomposition, frameworks, epistemic rigor) + **your portfolio patterns** (X-RAY skills, onboarding workflows, case studies) + **Anthropic standards** (Projects, Styles, Skills separation) into **reusable daily workflows** with **explicit decision rationale** and **practical examples per variable**.

Every response follows these 6 rules:

1. **Decomposition over decoration** — Variables, constraints, hypotheses, dependencies before solutions
2. **Framework routing** — Minimum sufficient lens (MECE, Inversion, JTBD, 5W2H), justified, exclusions noted
3. **Epistemic discipline** — Tag FACT | HYPOTHESIS | INFERENCE | GAP
4. **Concise structured** — 300-600w default, adjust per complexity
5. **Source of truth** — Cite inline, never fabricate, mark unknowns

    58	
    59	## DECISION: Hybrid Architecture (Best of Both)
    60	
    61	**Why not pure CMD v2 OR pure Diamond?**
    62	
    63	1. **CMD v2 alone** = Router without execution engine
    64	2. **Diamond alone** = Research-only, can't handle docs/code/analysis
    65	3. **Hybrid** = Intelligent router → delegates to specialized skills → learns from patterns
    66	
    67	Anthropic's subagent orchestration principle: "Claude can recognize when tasks would benefit from delegating work to specialized subagents and do so proactively"
    68	
    69	---
    70	
    71	## ARCHITECTURE: CMD v3 (Refined for Anthropic 2026)
    72	
    73	### Core Design Philosophy
    74	
    75	```yaml
    76	name: CMD v3 Orchestrator
    77	principle: "Complexity at capability layer, simplicity at interface layer"
    78	
    79	flow:
    80	  layer_1_intake: "3-question interactive Q&A (mandatory)"
    81	  layer_2_routing: "Cynefin + auto-inference → predict optimal path"
    82	  layer_3_execution: "Delegate to specialized skills (Diamond/docx/pptx/etc)"
    83	  layer_4_validation: "Quality gates + epistemic tags"
    84	  layer_5_delivery: "Structured output + next action + metadata"
    85	
    86	anthropic_compliance:
    87	  - effort: "max" # Per your selection
    88	  - thinking: {type: "adaptive"} # Let Claude decide when to reason deeply
    89	  - tools: "parallel_when_possible" # Speed via parallelization
    90	  - output: "XML structured + epistemic tags"
    91	  - verbosity: "Show all work (per your requirement)"
    92	```
    93	
    94	---
    95	
    96	## LAYER 1: Interactive Q&A (Mandatory Pre-Flight)
    97	
    98	**Anthropic-Compliant Version**:
    99	
   100	```xml
   101	<pre_flight_questionnaire>
   102	  <question id="q1_scope">
   103	    <prompt>What type of deliverable do you need?</prompt>
   104	    <options>
   105	      <option value="research">Research (market/competitive/validation)</option>
   106	      <option value="document">Document (report/presentation/spreadsheet)</option>
   107	      <option value="analysis">Analysis (data/code/strategy)</option>
   108	      <option value="creation">Creation (workflow/system/framework)</option>
   109	      <option value="hybrid">Hybrid (multi-phase project)</option>
   110	    </options>
   111	    <auto_inference>
   112	      <signal>Keywords like "research", "market", "validate" → auto-suggest "research"</signal>
   113	      <signal>".docx", "presentation", "report" → auto-suggest "document"</signal>
   114	      <display>Show predicted answer + confidence % → user confirms or overrides</display>
   115	    </auto_inference>
   116	  </question>
   117	
   118	  <question id="q2_depth">
   119	    <prompt>Reasoning depth required?</prompt>
   120	    <options>
   121	      <option value="cynefin_clear">Clear/Simple (execute directly, low ambiguity)</option>
   122	      <option value="cynefin_complicated">Complicated (expert analysis, multiple variables)</option>
   123	      <option value="cynefin_complex">Complex (emergent patterns, requires probing)</option>
   124	      <option value="cynefin_chaotic">Chaotic (rapid response, stabilize first)</option>
   125	    </options>
   126	    <auto_inference>
   127	      <method>Analyze request complexity via token count + ambiguity detection</method>
   128	      <cynefin_classifier>
   129	        - Clear: "<50 tokens, single deliverable, no trade-offs"
   130	        - Complicated: "50-200 tokens, multiple steps, expert domain"
   131	        - Complex: "200+ tokens, unknown unknowns, iterative discovery"
   132	        - Chaotic: "Crisis language, urgency signals, stabilization needed"
   133	      </cynefin_classifier>
   134	      <display>Show classification + reasoning → user confirms</display>
   135	    </auto_inference>
   136	  </question>
   137	
   138	  <question id="q3_quality_bar">
   139	    <prompt>Quality bar and delivery target?</prompt>
   140	    <options>
   141	      <option value="diamond">Diamond (publication-ready, 95%+ data verified, full epistemic tags)</option>
   142	      <option value="gold">Gold (production-ready, 85%+ data verified, key sources cited)</option>
   143	      <option value="silver">Silver (draft quality, 70%+ data verified, directional accuracy)</option>
   144	      <option value="bronze">Bronze (exploratory, 50%+ data verified, hypothesis generation)</option>
   145	    </options>
   146	    <auto_inference>
   147	      <signal>Stakes detection: "investor pitch", "client deliverable" → suggest Diamond</signal>
   148	      <signal>Speed signals: "quick", "draft", "rough" → suggest Silver/Bronze</signal>
   149	      <signal>Default for research specialist role → suggest Gold minimum</signal>
   150	      <display>Show suggested tier + effort estimate → user confirms</display>
[2631 lines total]
   150	      <display>Show suggested tier + effort estimate → user confirms</display>
   151	    </auto_inference>
   152	    <quality_mapping>
   153	      <diamond>
   154	        - Effort: max
   155	        - Sources: Primary only (company sites, academic, official docs)
   156	        - Validation: 3-source cross-check minimum
   157	        - Epistemic tags: FACT | HYPOTHESIS | INFERENCE | GAP on every claim
   158	        - Token budget: Unlimited (show all work)
   159	      </diamond>
   160	      <gold>
   161	        - Effort: xhigh
   162	        - Sources: Primary preferred, secondary acceptable with caveats
   163	        - Validation: 2-source cross-check
   164	        - Epistemic tags: On key claims only
   165	        - Token budget: High (detailed reasoning)
   166	      </gold>
   167	      <silver>
   168	        - Effort: high
   169	        - Sources: Mixed (flag confidence levels)
   170	        - Validation: 1-source minimum
   171	        - Epistemic tags: Summary level
   172	        - Token budget: Medium
   173	      </silver>
   174	      <bronze>
   175	        - Effort: medium
   176	        - Sources: Best available
   177	        - Validation: Directional only
   178	        - Epistemic tags: Optional
   179	        - Token budget: Standard
   180	      </bronze>
   181	    </quality_mapping>
   182	  </question>
   183	</pre_flight_questionnaire>
   184	```
   185	
   186	**User Experience**:
   187	
   188	```
   189	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   190	│ PRE-FLIGHT QUESTIONNAIRE                            │
   191	├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
   192	│                                                     │
   193	│ Q1: Deliverable Type?                              │
   194	│ ✓ Research (predicted from "market analysis")      │
   195	│   Document                                         │
   196	│   Analysis                                         │
   197	│   Creation                                         │
   198	│   Hybrid                                           │
   199	│                                                     │
   200	│ Q2: Reasoning Depth? (Cynefin Classification)      │
   201	│   Clear/Simple                                     │
   202	│ ✓ Complicated (predicted: expert domain + data)    │
   203	│   Complex                                          │
   204	│   Chaotic                                          │
   205	│                                                     │
   206	│ Q3: Quality Bar?                                   │
   207	│   Diamond (publication-ready, ~2hr effort)         │
   208	│ ✓ Gold (production-ready, ~45min effort)           │
   209	│   Silver (draft, ~20min effort)                    │
   210	│   Bronze (exploratory, ~10min effort)              │
   211	│                                                     │
   212	│ [Confirm Selections] [Override Predictions]        │
   213	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   214	```

   217	
   218	## LAYER 2: Cynefin Routing + Auto-Inference Engine
   219	
   220	**Post-Confirmation, Pre-Execution**:
   221	
   222	```xml
   223	<routing_engine>
   224	  <cynefin_delegation>
   225	    <clear_simple>
   226	      <action>Execute directly with native Claude tools</action>
   227	      <no_skill_needed>True</no_skill_needed>
   228	      <example>"What's 2+2?" → answer immediately</example>
   229	    </clear_simple>
   230	    
   231	    <complicated>
   232	      <action>Delegate to specialized skill</action>
   233	      <skill_selection>
   234	        <if condition="deliverable == research">research-protocol-diamond.zip</if>
   235	        <if condition="deliverable == document AND format == docx">docx skill</if>
   236	        <if condition="deliverable == document AND format == pptx">pptx skill</if>
   237	        <if condition="deliverable == document AND format == xlsx">xlsx skill</if>
   238	        <if condition="deliverable == analysis AND domain == code">Use thinking + tool_use</if>
   239	      </skill_selection>
   240	      <quality_enforcement>Map quality_bar (Diamond/Gold/Silver/Bronze) → effort param</quality_enforcement>
   241	    </complicated>
   242	    
   243	    <complex>
   244	      <action>Multi-phase workflow with subagents</action>
   245	      <approach>
   246	        1. Probe (exploratory research to surface unknowns)
   247	        2. Sense (pattern detection via Diamond DIAMANTE)
   248	        3. Respond (iterative execution with validation gates)
   249	      </approach>
   250	      <subagent_orchestration>
   251	        - Research subagent → Diamond protocol
   252	        - Synthesis subagent → Cross-reference findings
   253	        - Validation subagent → Quality gate enforcement
   254	      </subagent_orchestration>
   255	    </complex>
   256	    
   257	    <chaotic>
   258	      <action>Stabilize first, then reclassify</action>
   259	      <stabilization>
   260	        1. Extract immediate action (PRINTODAY equivalent)
   261	        2. Execute with low effort for speed
   262	        3. Establish baseline → reclassify as Complicated/Complex
   263	        4. Re-engage with proper depth
   264	      </stabilization>
   265	    </chaotic>
   266	  </cynefin_delegation>
   267	
   268	  <auto_inference_predictions>
   269	    <context_analysis>
   270	      <token_density>Request length / specificity ratio</token_density>
   271	      <domain_signals>Keywords mapping to skill domains</domain_signals>
   272	      <format_indicators>File extensions, deliverable types mentioned</format_indicators>
   273	      <urgency_markers>"Today", "ASAP", "urgent" vs "thorough", "comprehensive"</urgency_marker>
   274	      <quality_hints>"Client", "investor", "publication" vs "draft", "rough"</quality_hints>
   275	    </context_analysis>
   276	    
   277	    <prediction_display>
   278	      <format>
   279	        Auto-predicted: [CHOICE] (Confidence: XX%)
   280	        Reasoning: [1-line Cynefin justification]
   281	        Override: [Show alternative options]
   282	      </format>
   283	      <user_feedback_loop>
   284	        - If user overrides → learn pattern for future requests
   285	        - If user confirms → reinforce prediction model
   286	      </user_feedback_loop>
   287	    </prediction_display>
   288	  </auto_inference_predictions>
   289	</routing_engine>
   290	```
   291

   294	## LAYER 3: Execution Delegation (Skill Integration)
   295	
   296	**How CMD v3 Talks to Research Protocol Diamond**:
   297	
   298	```yaml
   299	# CMD v3 acts as orchestrator, Diamond executes research
   300	
   301	cmd_v3_to_diamond_handoff:
   302	  params_passed:
   303	    quality_bar: "gold" # From Q3
   304	    effort: "max" # From your selection
   305	    cynefin_context: "complicated" # From Q2
   306	    thinking: {type: "adaptive"}
   307	    
   308	  diamond_receives:
   309	    phase_1_pre_research: "Use 3P normalized_request from CMD v3 context"
   310	    phase_2_diamante: "Execute full 8-layer decomposition"
   311	    phase_3_research: "Search with primary sources priority (per Gold quality bar)"
   312	    phase_4_output: "Structure per Diamond template (Q&A + options + action)"
   313	    phase_5_printoday: "Return executable action"
   314	    
   315	  cmd_v3_post_processing:
   316	    add_metadata:
   317	      classification: "Gold"
   318	      effort_used: "max"
   319	      token_count: "[actual]"
   320	      sources_verified: "[count]"
   321	      epistemic_breakdown: "X facts, Y hypotheses, Z inferences, W gaps"
   322	    
   323	    next_action_router:
   324	      if: "User satisfied"
   325	      then: "Save to Google Drive with metadata"
   326	      
   327	      if: "User requests iteration"
   328	      then: "Re-engage Diamond with refined params"
   329	      
   330	      if: "User requests different deliverable"
   331	      then: "Route to appropriate skill (docx/pptx/etc)"
   332	```

   348	      <format>In-text citation minimum</format>
   349	      <check>Key claims → SOURCE tag</check>
   350	    </gold_tier>
   351	  </gate_1_source_verification>

	< truncated lines 353-397 >

   485	## Token Philosophy: "Show All Work" Mode
   486	
   487	**Your Requirement**: "Max intelligence, detailed reasoning, show all work"
   488	
   489	**Anthropic Compliance**:
   490	
   491	```yaml
   492	effort_configuration:
   493	  level: "max"
   494	  thinking: {type: "adaptive"}
   495	  max_tokens: 64000 # Per Anthropic recommendation for max effort
   496	  
   497	reasoning_transparency:
   498	  - Show Cynefin classification logic
   499	  - Display auto-inference predictions + confidence
   500	  - Expose skill selection reasoning
   501	  - Include full DIAMANTE decomposition
   502	  - List all sources checked (even rejected ones)
   503	  - Document trade-off analysis
   504	  - Flag epistemic uncertainty explicitly
   505	  
   506	token_budget_display:
   507	  format: "Live counter after each major phase"
   508	  example: |
   509	    [Phase 1 Complete] Tokens: 2,341 | Remaining: 61,659
   510	    [Phase 2 Complete] Tokens: 5,892 | Remaining: 58,108
   511	    [Phase 3 Complete] Tokens: 12,847 | Remaining: 51,153
   512	```
   513	
   514	**Anti-Pattern Avoided**: Not "verbose for the sake of verbose" but "comprehensive reasoning when complexity warrants it"

   521	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

   524	                              │

   528	│ ┌─────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐         │
   529	│ │ Q1: Type    │  │ Q2: Cynefin  │  │ Q3: Quality Bar │         │
   530	│ │ (Research)  │→ │ (Complicated)│→ │ (Gold)          │         │
   531	│ └─────────────┘  └──────────────┘  └─────────────────┘         │
   532	│      ↓ Auto-inference predicts + user confirms                 │
   533	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   534	                              │
   535	                              ▼
   536	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   537	│ LAYER 2: Cynefin Router + Skill Delegation                     │
   538	│                                                                 │
   539	│  Clear/Simple → Direct execution (no skill)                    │
   540	│  Complicated  → Delegate to specialist skill ────────┐         │
   541	│  Complex      → Multi-phase subagent workflow        │         │
   542	│  Chaotic      → Stabilize → reclassify              │         │
   543	└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────┘
   544	                                                       │
   545	                              ┌────────────────────────┘
   546	                              ▼
   547	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   548	│ LAYER 3: Specialized Skills (Execution Engines)                │
   549	│                                                                 │
   550	│  ┌──────────────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐ │
   551	│  │ Research Protocol    │  │ Document     │  │ Data         │ │
   552	│  │ Diamond              │  │ Skills       │  │ Analysis     │ │
   553	│  │ (Your uploaded zip)  │  │ (docx/pptx)  │  │ (native)     │ │
   554	│  └──────────────────────┘  └──────────────┘  └──────────────┘ │
   555	│           ↓                        ↓                  ↓        │
   556	│  5-phase DIAMANTE exec    Format creation    Tool use chain   │
   557	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   558	                              │
   559	                              ▼
   560	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   561	│ LAYER 4: Quality Validation Gates                              │
   562	│                                                                 │
   563	│  ✓ Source verification (95% primary for Diamond)               │
   564	│  ✓ Epistemic tagging (FACT|HYPOTHESIS|INFERENCE|GAP)           │
   565	│  ✓ Trade-off transparency (choosing A loses X from B)          │
   566	│  ✓ No-inference limits (explicit gaps documented)              │
   567	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   568	                              │
   569	                              ▼
   570	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   571	│ LAYER 5: Structured Delivery                                   │
   572	│                                                                 │
   573	│  <cmd_v3_delivery>                                             │
   574	│    <metadata> effort=max, tokens=X, classification=Gold        │
   575	│    <executive_summary> 1-sentence + recommendation             │
   576	│    <detailed_output> Full skill output (Diamond YAML)          │
   577	│    <quality_report> Epistemic breakdown, sources, trade-offs   │
   578	│    <next_actions> PRINTODAY + done_definition                  │
   579	│    <file_delivery> Google Drive MCP integration                │
   580	│  </cmd_v3_delivery>                                            │
   581	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

   586	## BUILD DECISION
   587	
   588	**3 Options**:
   589	
   590	**A) Full System Prompt** (10-15K tokens, global instructions)  
   591	**B) SKILL.md Package** (portable, uploadable, reusable)  
   592	**C) Hybrid** (lightweight prompt + skills library)
   593	
   594	**Recommendation for Research Specialist Role**: **Option C (Hybrid)**
   595	
   596	**Why**: Anthropic's skill-based architecture allows "Claude to discover state from the local filesystem" and "skills encode environment-specific constraints" — better than monolithic prompts.

  1253	## 🧠 CRITICAL INSIGHT FROM THIS CONVERSATION
  1254	
  1255	**What actually happened here** (anatomy of the process to clone):
  1256	
  1257	```mermaid
  1258	sequenceDiagram
  1259	    participant U as User (rough input)
  1260	    participant E as Extraction Layer
  1261	    participant R as Routing Layer
  1262	    participant T as Transform Layer
  1263	    participant D as Delivery Layer
  1264	    
  1265	    U->>E: Typo-heavy, multi-layer request
  1266	    E->>E: Normalize explicit vs implicit
  1267	    E->>E: Extract: decisions, reasoning, architecture, context
  1268	    E->>R: Structured payload
  1269	    R->>R: Cynefin classify
  1270	    R->>R: Who is the audience?
  1271	    R->>T: Route to format(s)
  1272	    T->>T: Transform for audience
  1273	    T->>D: Case study / skill / publication
  1274	    D->>U: Multi-format delivery
  1275	```
  1276	
  1277	**The insight**: The value is NOT the extraction. It's the **transformation routing** — same raw content → different outputs for different audiences.
  1278

  1340	
  1341	```yaml
  1342	extraction_layers:
  1343	  L1_surface:
  1344	    what: "Explicit requests + responses"
  1345	    example: "User asked for CMD v3, Claude built it"

  1348	    what: "Decision logic + why choices were made"

  1355	  L4_meta:
  1356	    what: "Pattern analysis + reusable frameworks"

  1363	
  1364	### Failure Mode Mitigations
  1365	
  1366	|Failure Mode|Mitigation Strategy|Implementation|
  1367	|---|---|---|
  1368	|**F1: Context collapse**|Chunked extraction (20K token segments)|`recent_chats` + `conversation_search` tools|
  1369	|**F2: Hallucination**|Tag all reconstructed reasoning as `INFERENCE`|Epistemic tagging required|
  1370	|**F3: Format mismatch**|Separate data model per format|Schema-first design|
  1371	|**F4: Overkill**|3 engines max, no nested routers|Flat architecture|
  1372	|**F5: Live vs Retro**|Two modes, one skill, explicit switch|`mode: live|
  1373	|**F6: Audience confusion**|Ask once, route all simultaneously|Parallel transformation|
  1374	|**F7: Token bankruptcy**|Budget gating per extraction phase|30K max per engine|
  1375

     1	# CMD-05-COLECTOR
     2	## Daily Intake · Index · Self-Update System
     3	
     4	```
     5	name: CMD-05-COLECTOR
     6	version: 1.0.0
     7	aliases: COLECTOR / "colector" / C05
     8	daily-mode: true
     9	chain: collector → inline JSON → #META-REGENERATION → skill-creator → BACKLOG.md
    10	```
    11	
    12	---
    13	
    14	## DESIGN PHILOSOPHY — Built for Daily Use
    15	
    16	Three rules that drove every decision:
    17	
    18	1. **One trigger, runs to completion.** No interruptions mid-flow. User drops files, types "colector", comes back to a done state.
    19	2. **Never block on ambiguity.** Unclassified files go to `_inbox/`, session continues. Nothing waits on a classification decision.
    20	3. **Chat context is the pipe.** The inline JSON output is already in the conversation. skill-creator reads it from context — no extra Drive reads, no re-fetching.
    21	
    22	---
    23	
    24	## SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE
    25	
    26	```
    27	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    28	│                    USER INPUT                           │
    29	│          files in chat / path / uploaded ZIP            │
    30	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    31	                          ↓
    32	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    33	│                  PHASE 1 — INIT                         │
    34	│  Read manifest.yaml from Drive (lightweight, not XLS)   │
    35	│  Check session lock → detect orphan sessions            │
    36	│  Write session-lock.json to Drive                       │
    37	│  Load: normalization rules + family taxonomy            │
    38	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    39	                          ↓
    40	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    41	│                 PHASE 2 — NORMALIZE                     │
    42	│  Single LLM call: all filenames → normalized IDs        │
    43	│  Grammar: [FAMILY]-[TYPE]-[SEQ] (e.g. XR-DOC-014)      │
    44	│  Unclassified → INBOX-[SEQ], flagged not blocked        │
    45	│  Delta check: skip already-indexed IDs                  │
    46	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    47	                          ↓
    48	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    49	│                 PHASE 3 — STRUCTURE                     │
    50	│  Generate: master README + 5W2H tabular                 │
    51	│  Generate: group READMEs for each family detected       │
    52	│  Copy files into folder hierarchy by family             │
    53	│  Build ZIP                                              │
    54	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    55	                          ↓
    56	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    57	│                 PHASE 4 — COMMIT                        │
    58	│  Snapshot current XLS → backup-YYYYMMDD.xlsx in Drive   │
    59	│  Append new rows to master XLS (never overwrite)        │
    60	│  Write manifest.yaml back to Drive (ground truth)       │
    61	│  Upload ZIP to Drive delivery folder                    │
    62	│  Remove session-lock.json                               │
    63	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    64	                          ↓
    65	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    66	│              PHASE 5 — OUTPUT INLINE JSON               │
    67	│  Emit structured JSON block directly in chat            │
    68	│  JSON is the handoff payload — already in context       │
    69	│  Present ZIP via present_files                          │
    70	└─────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘
    71	                          ↓
    72	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    73	│           PHASE 6 — #META-REGENERATION                  │
    74	│  skill-creator reads inline JSON from context           │
    75	│  Extracts backlog_signal field                          │
    76	│  One-line confirm: "Adding to BACKLOG: [signal]. OK?"   │
    77	│  Appends entry to BACKLOG.md in Drive                   │
    78	│  Done                                                   │
    79	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
    80	```
    81	
    82	---
    83	
    84	## INLINE JSON CONTRACT — v1.0
    85	
    86	The shape the collector always outputs. Versioned so skill-creator
    87	can handle future changes without breaking.
    88	
    89	```json
    90	{
    91	  "schema_version": "1.0",
    92	  "session_id": "C05-20260509-001",
    93	  "timestamp": "2026-05-09T14:30:00Z",
    94	
    95	  "stats": {
    96	    "files_received": 12,
    97	    "files_processed": 10,
    98	    "files_unclassified": 2,
    99	    "ids_assigned": 10,
   100	    "delta_skipped": 0,
   101	    "drive_uploads": 10
   102	  },
   103	
   104	  "items": [
   105	    {
   106	      "id": "XR-DOC-014",
   107	      "raw_name": "Leo consultant brief may9.docx",
   108	      "normalized_name": "xr-doc-014-consultant-brief-may.docx",
   109	      "family": "DOC",
   110	      "drive_link": "https://drive.google.com/file/d/...",
   111	      "xls_row": 14,
   112	      "status": "indexed"
   113	    }
   114	  ],
   115	
   116	  "unclassified": [
   117	    {
   118	      "raw_name": "random-thing.jsx",
   119	      "inbox_id": "INBOX-003",
   120	      "reason": "no mappable family for .jsx extension"
   121	    }
   122	  ],
   123	
   124	  "backlog_signal": "normalization-rules missing .jsx → consider adding FORGE family mapping",
   125	
   126	  "delivery": {
   127	    "zip_name": "collection-C05-20260509-001.zip",
   128	    "drive_zip_link": "https://drive.google.com/file/d/...",
   129	    "xls_row_range": "14–23",
   130	    "manifest_version": "v47"
   131	  }
   132	}
   133	```
   134	
   135	**Rules:**
   136	- `backlog_signal` is always a single actionable string or `null`
   137	- `items` only contains files processed this session (delta)
   138	- `stats.delta_skipped` shows files already in manifest, not reprocessed
   139	- `unclassified` never blocks — session completes regardless
   140	
   141	---
   142	
   143	## #META-REGENERATION — Internal CMD
   144	
   145	Fires automatically after Phase 5. Encoded inside SKILL.md
   146	so it is always part of the workflow, not optional.
   147	
   148	```
   149	#META-REGENERATION
   150	
   151	TRIGGER: automatic — fires after inline JSON is emitted
   152	INPUT: inline JSON already visible in conversation context
   153	         (no Drive read, no re-fetch — data is already here)
   154	
   155	STEPS:
   156	  1. skill-creator reads JSON from context
   157	  2. Checks backlog_signal field
   158	     → if null: append minimal session log only
   159	     → if present: include signal as improvement note
   160	  3. Confirm with user (one line):
   161	     "BACKLOG entry ready: [signal or session-id]. Confirm?"
   162	  4. User says yes (or is silent for 10s → auto-confirm)
   163	  5. Append entry to BACKLOG.md in Drive [BACKLOG_FILE_ID]
   164	  6. Return: "✓ BACKLOG updated — entry C05-20260509-001"
   165	
   166	BACKLOG ENTRY FORMAT:
   167	  ## C05-20260509-001 · 2026-05-09
   168	  - Files: 10 indexed, 2 to inbox
   169	  - Families: DOC, SKILL, HTML
   170	  - Signal: normalization-rules missing .jsx → FORGE mapping
   171	  - XLS rows: 14–23
   172	
   173	CONSTRAINT: do NOT modify SKILL.md or any skill file.
   174	            Append BACKLOG.md only. One entry per session.
   175	```
   176

   179	## ACTION ID TAXONOMY
   180	
   181	### ACTIONS (A01–A20)
   182	
   183	| ID | Name | Phase | Description | Time |
   184	|----|------|-------|-------------|------|
   185	| **A01** | Init Session | 1 | Read manifest.yaml from Drive | 3s |
   186	| **A02** | Check Lock | 1 | Detect orphan sessions, write new lock | 2s |
   187	| **A03** | Load Rules | 1 | Read normalization-rules + family taxonomy | 2s |
   188	| **A04** | Normalize Batch | 2 | Single LLM call: all filenames → IDs | 10s |
   189	| **A05** | Delta Detect | 2 | Compare batch against manifest, skip dupes | 3s |
   190	| **A06** | Route Inbox | 2 | Move unclassified to _inbox/ with INBOX-ID | 2s |
   191	| **A07** | Generate README | 3 | Master README from collection metadata | 12s |
   192	| **A08** | Generate 5W2H | 3 | 5W2H tabular for the collection | 8s |
   193	| **A09** | Generate Group READMEs | 3 | One README per detected family | 8s |
   194	| **A10** | Build Folder Structure | 3 | Copy files into family hierarchy | 3s |
   195	| **A11** | Build ZIP | 3 | Package structured output | 3s |
   196	| **A12** | Snapshot XLS | 4 | Backup current XLS before write | 3s |
   197	| **A13** | Append XLS Rows | 4 | Write new rows (append-only, never overwrite) | 5s |
   198	| **A14** | Write Manifest | 4 | Push manifest.yaml to Drive (ground truth) | 3s |
   199	| **A15** | Upload ZIP | 4 | Push ZIP to Drive delivery folder | 4s |
   200	| **A16** | Release Lock | 4 | Remove session-lock.json from Drive | 1s |
[481 lines total]
   200	| **A16** | Release Lock | 4 | Remove session-lock.json from Drive | 1s |
   201	| **A17** | Emit JSON | 5 | Output inline JSON block in chat | 2s |
   202	| **A18** | Meta-Regeneration | 6 | Fire #META-REGENERATION → skill-creator | 15s |
   203	| **A19** | Resolve Inbox | — | User-triggered: classify INBOX items | varies |
   204	| **A20** | Rollback Session | — | Restore from snapshot, remove orphan lock | 10s |

   241	
   242	## DATA LOSS PREVENTION — 4 Layers
   243	
   244	```
   245	Layer 1 — APPEND ONLY
   246	  XLS rows are never modified or deleted.
   247	  Re-classified files get a new row with updated info.
   248	  Old row gets deprecated=true flag. History preserved.
   249	
   250	Layer 2 — MANIFEST AS GROUND TRUTH
   251	  manifest.yaml is the canonical index.
   252	  XLS is derived from it.
   253	  If XLS gets corrupted: run A08 → XLS regenerated from manifest.
   254	  Manifest is small (plain text YAML) — never corrupted by Excel bugs.
   255	
   256	Layer 3 — SNAPSHOT BEFORE WRITE
   257	  A12 runs before every A13.
   258	  Creates: master-index-backup-YYYYMMDD.xlsx in Drive.
   259	  Drive also keeps version history — double safety net.
   260	
   261	Layer 4 — SESSION LOCK
   262	  INIT writes session-lock.json with session_id + timestamp.
   263	  COMMIT deletes it.
   264	  Next INIT checks for existing lock:
   265	    → lock older than 2h = orphan session detected
   266	    → shows what was uploaded in orphan session
   267	    → offers: "complete commit" or "rollback"
   268	  Prevents silent data divergence between Drive files and XLS.
   269	```
   270	
   271	---
   272	
   273	## PERFORMANCE FEATURES
   274	
   275	```
   276	NORMALIZATION AS GRAMMAR (not LLM per file)
   277	  Deterministic rules in normalization-rules.md:
   278	    [FAMILY-PREFIX]-[TYPE]-[SEQ]
   279	    XR-DOC-014, XR-SKILL-003, XR-HTML-007
   280	  LLM only invoked when family cannot be determined.
   281	  Result: 10 files normalized in one call, not 10 calls.
   282	
   283	MANIFEST OVER XLS FOR INIT
   284	  manifest.yaml ≈ 5KB for 500 items.
   285	  XLS ≈ 500KB+ for same.
   286	  Init reads manifest. XLS only touched at commit.
   287	  Result: init is 10× faster on large collections.
   288	
   289	DELTA BY DEFAULT
   290	  manifest stores all indexed IDs.
   291	  New session: compare input against manifest → skip known IDs.
   292	  Re-sending same batch costs near zero.
   293	  Result: idempotent runs. Safe to re-trigger without damage.
   294	
   295	SINGLE LLM CALL FOR ALL DOCS
   296	  README-MASTER + 5W2H + group READMEs = one structured prompt.
   297	  Output: JSON with all three docs as fields.
   298	  Parsed and written to files in one pass.
   299	  Result: 3 documents for the cost of 1 LLM call.
   300	
   301	AMBIGUITY NEVER BLOCKS
   302	  Unclassified file → INBOX-[SEQ] immediately.
   303	  Session continues without waiting for user input.
   304	  Inbox items listed in JSON output.
   305	  User resolves later with T04.
   306	  Result: zero interruptions during daily run.
   307	```
   308	
   309	---
   310	
   311	## DRIVE FOLDER STRUCTURE (fixed hierarchy)
   312	
   313	```
   314	📁 X-RAY-SYSTEM/
   315	├── 📁 _manifest/
   316	│   ├── manifest.yaml              ← ground truth index
   317	│   ├── session-lock.json          ← written at INIT, deleted at COMMIT
   318	│   └── backups/
   319	│       └── manifest-YYYYMMDD.yaml ← session snapshots
   320	│
   321	├── 📁 _index/
   322	│   ├── master-index.xlsx          ← XLS with Drive links (append-only)
   323	│   └── backups/
   324	│       └── master-index-backup-YYYYMMDD.xlsx
   325	│
   326	├── 📁 _delivery/
   327	│   └── collection-C05-[session-id].zip
   328	│
   329	├── 📁 _inbox/
   330	│   └── [unclassified files]       ← INBOX-001, INBOX-002...
   331	│
   332	├── 📁 DOC/                        ← family folders (auto-created)
   333	├── 📁 SKILL/
   334	├── 📁 HTML/
   335	├── 📁 PROMPT/
   336	├── 📁 SCRIPT/
   337	└── 📁 [other families]/
   338	```
   339	
   340	All folder IDs stored in `references/drive-config.md`.
   341	Folder IDs never change. File moves don't break links.
   342	
   343	---
   344	
   345	## XLS MASTER INDEX — Sheet Structure
   346	
   347	```
   348	Sheet: INDEX (main)
   349	  Col A: ID             XR-DOC-014
   350	  Col B: normalized_name xr-doc-014-consultant-brief-may.docx
   351	  Col C: raw_name       Leo consultant brief may9.docx
   352	  Col D: family         DOC
   353	  Col E: drive_link     =HYPERLINK(base_url&A2, "Open")
   354	  Col F: session_id     C05-20260509-001
   355	  Col G: date           2026-05-09
   356	  Col H: status         indexed / deprecated / inbox
   357	  Col I: notes          (free text)
   358	
   359	Sheet: CONFIG
   360	  next_id_seq           14         ← incremented each session, written back
   361	  base_drive_url        https://drive.google.com/file/d/
   362	  last_session          C05-20260509-001
   363	  manifest_version      v47
   364	
   365	Sheet: SESSIONS
   366	  One row per session — session_id, date, files_added, backlog_signal
   367	
   368	Sheet: INBOX
   369	  Unclassified items — inbox_id, raw_name, reason, date, resolved (bool)
   370	```
   371	
   372	HYPERLINK formula uses `CONFIG!base_drive_url` so if the base ever changes,
   373	one cell update propagates to all links.

PORTIFOLIO
Research + data validation | Separate FACT / INFERENCE / HYPOTHESIS / GAP. Web search for current evidence. Code for computation. |
| 6. Output governance | Executive summary + decision table + CMD final + risks + next actions |
| 7. ROI + quality measurement | Time saved, iterations reduced, acceptance rate, evidence coverage |

**Golden rule:** Simple tasks → simple answers. Repeatable tasks → become skills. Evidence-required tasks → trigger search. Sensitive deliverables → QA gate.

### 4.2 Adversarial Filter (CMD-06 v2) — Portfolio Decisions

Default state: TRASH. Every idea must prove survival.

**Hard Gates — all must pass. One fail = KILL.**

| Gate | Requirement |
|------|------------|
| HK1 — Anthropic-aligned | Cited + reasoned, not asserted |
| HK2 — Original (90-day) | Date-stamped search with result links |
| HK3 — Used 7+ days personally | Drive timestamps, chat history |
| HK4 — Solo-buildable before Sep 2026 | Concrete scope + time estimate |

**Soft Gates — scored 0/1/2. Need ≥8/14 to survive.**

| Gate | Criteria |
|------|---------|
| SK1 — Customer evidence | 0=hypothetical, 1=1-2 named, 2=3+ with friction |
| SK2 — Outcome evidence | 0=none, 1=anecdotal, 2=numbers |
| SK3 — Defensibility | 0=Anthropic kills it, 2=uniquely valuable |
| SK4 — Composability | Fits CMD taxonomy |
| SK5 — Adversarial survival | Survived hostile critique |
| SK6 — Concept clarity | Explainable in 1 sentence |
| SK7 — Naming asset | Sharp, memorable name |

**Verdict scale:**
- All HK + SK ≥ 12 → KEEP-PUBLISH (show to Anthropic)
- All HK + SK 8–11 → KEEP-BUILD
- All HK + SK 4–7 → INCUBATE (private notes, no claims)
- Any HK fail → KILL immediately

### 4.3 Cynefin Router — Energy Allocation

After surviving the filter, each idea gets a domain score (1–15) from three multiplied dimensions:

- **Q1** Originality (1–5): 1=documented, 5=no one has seen this
- **Q2** Window tightness (1–5): 1=years, 5=weeks before someone beats you
- **Q3** Strategic value (1–5): 1=nice-to-have, 5=changes reputation/income/direction

| Score | Domain | Action | Energy |
|-------|--------|--------|--------|
| 1–3 | Obvious | Use internally, no public claim | 0h |
| 4–6 | Complicated | Tutorial or reference doc | 2h |
| 7–11 | Complex | Concept paper + validation sprint | 1 week |
| 12–15 | Pioneer | Immediate sprint + public claim | 7-day focus |
